It has its roots in 1940s and 1950s rock and roll and rockabilly, which evolved from blues, country music and other influences. According to the All Music Guide, In its purest form, Rock &amp; Roll has three chords, a strong, insistent back beat, and a catchy melody.  Early rock &amp; roll drew from a variety of sources, primarily blues, R&amp;B, and country, but also gospel, traditional pop, jazz, and folk. All of these influences combined in a simple, blues-based song structure that was fast, danceable, and catchy.','Rock music is a genre of music started in America. It has its roots in 1940s and 1950s rock and roll and rockabilly, which evolved from blues, country music and other influences. According to the All Music Guide, In its purest form, Rock &amp; Roll has three chords, a strong, insistent back beat, and a catchy melody.  Early rock &amp; roll drew from a variety of sources, primarily blues, R&amp;B, and country, but also gospel, traditional pop, jazz, and folk. All of these influences combined in a simple, blues-based song structure that was fast, danceable, and catchy. Rock usually has a prominent vocal melody, accompanied by guitar, drums, and bass. Many styles of rock music also use keyboard instruments such as organ, piano, mellotron, and synthesizers. Other instruments sometimes utilized in rock include saxophone (originally in the 50s the central instrument), harmonica, violin, flute, French horn, banjo, melodica, and timpani. Also, less common stringed instruments such as mandolin and sitar are used. Rock music usually has a strong back beat, and often revolves around the guitar, either solid electric, hollow electric, or acoustic.
 
 In the late 1960s, rock music was blended with folk music to create folk rock, blues to create blues-rock and with jazz, to create jazz-rock fusion, and without a time signature to create psychedelic rock. In the 1970s, rock incorporated influences from soul, funk, and latin music. Also in the 1970s, rock developed a number of subgenres, such as soft rock, heavy metal, hard rock, progressive rock, and punk rock. Rock subgenres that emerged in the 1980s included synthpop, hardcore punk and alternative rock. In the 1990s, rock subgenres included grunge, Britpop, indie rock, and nu metal.
 
 A group of musicians specializing in rock music is called a rock band or rock group. Many rock groups consist of a guitarist, lead singer, bass guitarist, and drummer, forming a quartet. Some groups omit one or more of these roles and/or utilize a lead singer who plays an instrument while singing, forming a trio or duo; others include additional musicians such as one or two rhythm guitarists and/or a keyboardist. More rarely, groups also utilize stringed instruments such as violins or cellos, and/or horns like saxophones, trumpets or trombones.')

','A &quot;type of dance music, played on electronic instruments and with a slow beat&quot;, according to Longman Dictionary, <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/trip-hop" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">trip-hop</a> (also known in the past as the &quot;Bristol sound&quot;) is, in fact, a musical movement that started in Bristol, UK. The tag isn%27t limited to Bristol-based bands though; bands as far as Canada (eg. <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Perfume+Tree" class="bbcode_artist">Perfume Tree</a>) or Costa Rica (eg. <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/%C3%9Aztari" class="bbcode_artist">&Uacute;ztari</a>) have been considered %27trip-hop%27.  Many %27trip-hop%27 bands like <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Massive+Attack" class="bbcode_artist">Massive Attack</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Portishead" class="bbcode_artist">Portishead</a> or <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Tricky" class="bbcode_artist">Tricky</a> have denied the term though, claiming it to be &quot;an invention of media journalists&quot;. (It was in fact coined by Luke Vibert aka Wagon Christ).
 
 Trip-hop music is widely considered to be part of electronic music. However, unlike most sub-genres of electronic music, trip-hop has a mostly organic sound that rarely puts emphasis on electronic instruments. At first, bands like Portishead have been considered %27<a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/alternative%20rock" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">alternative rock</a>%27 in the lack of a term like trip-hop; however, the message of most trip-hop music is different from the message of most <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/rock" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">rock</a> music. Also, guitars aren%27t used often and, when they are used, they are used in a moderate proportion, whilst drums and vocals are the main instruments. Trip-hop couldn%27t be considered <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/pop" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">pop</a> music, as most trip-hop music hasn%27t reached enough popularity, while popular bands like <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Massive+Attack" class="bbcode_artist">Massive Attack</a> aren%27t associated with pop music.
 
 Trip-hop is considered to be a very abused tag, used for artists that couldn%27t be considered %27trip-hop%27. After the initial success generated by <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Portishead" class="bbcode_artist">Portishead</a>%27s Dummy album, in the mid-/late %2790s discussion took place on the subject of so-called %27trip-hop%27 bands using the Portishead formula without presenting enough innovations to be considered not clones. In reality, very few bands replicated the exact Portishead sound; there were many pop-oriented bands who didn%27t used the %27cabaret noir%27 elements of the Portishead sound, for instance, often resulting in a sound that resembles <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Morcheeba" class="bbcode_artist">Morcheeba</a> or <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Hooverphonic" class="bbcode_artist">Hooverphonic</a>. Even so, many such bands presented special elements or contributions that made them overcome the %27Portishead clone%27 tag and enter the ranks of trip-hop databases such as <a href="http://tripofagia.sites.uol.com.br/tripofagia-1024-en.htm" rel="nofollow">Tripofagia</a> or <a href="http://www.tripnotic.de/" rel="nofollow">Tripnotic</a>.
 
 At most of the artists/bands of this movement, <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/hip-hop" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">hip-hop</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/dub" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">dub</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/reggae" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">reggae</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/techno" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">techno</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/rock" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">rock</a>and <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/pop" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">pop</a> could be identified. However, being a musical movement, not a fully fleshed out sub-genre, it is hard to identify a recipe for all trip-hop artists. Most comm')

The term &quot;Chill out music&quot;, as well as the genre itself, originated in chill rooms that were set up by DJs off to the edge of club dance floors to give patrons a chance to take a break from the hectic dance vibe and chill out with this style of music.','Chill out (sometimes also chillout, chill-out, or simply chill), a term derived from a slang injunction to relax, emerged in the early and mid-1990s as a catch-all term for various styles of relatively mellow, slow-tempo music made by contemporary producers in the electronic music scene. The term &quot;Chill out music&quot;, as well as the genre itself, originated in chill rooms that were set up by DJs off to the edge of club dance floors to give patrons a chance to take a break from the hectic dance vibe and chill out with this style of music. Chill out as a musical genre or descriptive is synonymous with the more recently popularized terms &quot;smooth electronica&quot; and &quot;soft techno&quot; and is a loose genre of music blurring into several other very distinct styles of electronic and lo-fi music.
 
 Notable artists
 
 Although chill out is an emerging - however loose - genre of music, it is quite robust and features many prolific artists. Throughout the 1990s and the current decade, there have been many artists who have made a significant impact on what has come to be known as &quot;chill out music&quot; today. Among the most notable of those artists and projects are (in no order of precedence): Air, Fila Brazillia, Kruder &amp; Dorfmeister, dZihan &amp; Kamien, Thievery Corporation, Sven Van Hees, Lemongrass, Tosca, Ganga, Monte La Rue, Nightmares on Wax, The Dining Rooms, Bluetech, Sounds from the Ground, Jens Buchert, A Man Called Adam, Electric Skychurch, Mystical Sun, Single Cell Orchestra, Alex Cortiz, Zero 7, Sia, Boards of Canada, Stidiek. William Orbit, Groove Armada, Leftfield, Lenny Ibizarre, Timonkey, Banco de Gaia, Alan Steward and Lemon Jelly.')

The beat is sometimes made from loops that have a hypnotic feeling. Sometimes the beats are more complicated and more featured instead of being in the background, but even then they are usually less intense than other kinds of electronic music like Trance.   ','Downtempo (or Downbeat) is a laid-back electronic music style similar to ambient music, but usually with a beat or groove unlike the beatless forms of Ambient music. The beat is sometimes made from loops that have a hypnotic feeling. Sometimes the beats are more complicated and more featured instead of being in the background, but even then they are usually less intense than other kinds of electronic music like Trance. 
 
 Often the name chill out music is used to refer to songs demonstrative of the genre, but those names also refer to other styles of music, and downtempo encompasses a wider variety of styles than those terms alone would indicate. 
 Another related genre is Trip hop, though Downtempo usually uses a slower tempo than Trip-hop. Due to the relaxing and often sensual or romantic feel of most downtempo music, along with the absence or minimal use of lyrics or vocals, it is a popular form of background music in %27chill out rooms%27 of dance parties, many alternative cafes, and is often marketed as being good music for lovemaking.

It has all the characteristics of it%27s Emo and Punk roots, like a DIY ethic, and normally lo-fi production for example, but is more aggressive and chaotic than Emo, characterized with harsh, screamed vocals (duh) and experimental instrumentation. Some bands of this genre may employ odd tempo changes and other techniques, twinkly breakdowns, and generally have very fast paced and high-energy shows. The subject matter of Screamo is very broad, and more abstract, often with intelligent and poetic lyrics.','An off-shoot of Emotive Hardcore, or Emo for short, Screamo surfaced in the 90%27s, primarily. It has all the characteristics of it%27s Emo and Punk roots, like a DIY ethic, and normally lo-fi production for example, but is more aggressive and chaotic than Emo, characterized with harsh, screamed vocals (duh) and experimental instrumentation. Some bands of this genre may employ odd tempo changes and other techniques, twinkly breakdowns, and generally have very fast paced and high-energy shows. The subject matter of Screamo is very broad, and more abstract, often with intelligent and poetic lyrics. The Screamo scene is still alive today, especially in Europe.')

 <strong>1)</strong> Philippe Katerine (known as <strong>Katerine</strong> for his artistic work) is a French singer and composer, who published eight records since the beginning of his career in 1991.
 He was born in 1968.
 
 
 <strong>2)</strong> <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Katerine+Avgoustakis" class="bbcode_artist">Katerine Avgoustakis</a> is a Belgian singer and was the winner of the 2005 Belgian Star Academy, similar to American Idol in the United States. She was born on September 16, 1983, to a Greek father and a Belgian mother.
 
 Currently, she lives in Maasmechelen. Avgoustakis used to be a beauty specialist and before that a saleswoman. During the third quarter of 2005, it was announced that Avgoustakis had been dating Pim Symoens, who was #4 in Star Academy and who also works for JIMtv, a popular Flemish music channel.
 
 Avgoustakis plays the piano and used to be in a choir. She was also a member of her first band Indiana, with whom she participated with for Eurovision Song Contest a couple of years ago, with the song Imitation Love.
 
 Due to the failure of Indiana, she entered Star Academy in Flanders. In 2005, she worked her way to the finale and won the contest and a record contract. Avgoustakis%27s debut single New Day, released in July 2005 in Belgium, peaked at #2 in the Belgian UltraTop 50 chart. &quot;New Day&quot; was written and produced by Regi Penxten &amp; Filip Vandueren, the team behind Milk Inc. Three months later, she received the TMF Flanders award for Best New National Artist for the song. Also the song was certified gold in Belgium. Her selfnamed debut album Katerine was released on November 14, 2005 in Belgium. The album is to be released in May in the Netherlands. Due the %27unexpected%27 sudden death of her mother, her second single, Here Come All the Boys, was delayed to be released in October 2005. This is the first single she also released in the Netherlands, that peaked at #89 in the Dutch Mega Singles Top 100. The song is also featured on the hits compilation HitBox, which was released on March 13, 2006, containing hits like Ricky Martin%27s I Don%27t Care, Rihanna%27s If It%27s Lovin%27 That You Want and the Michael Jackson cover Say Say Say (Waiting 4 U) by Hi_Tack.
 
 Avgoustakis won the first Belgian pre-selection for Eurosong 2006 on January 8, 2006 with the song Watch Me Move. Because of this, she was sure to have a place in the pre-finale rounds, however the judges thought her voice wasn%27t powerful enough to win. Despite being considered as one of the finalists, Katerine remained in the semi. 
 
 The third single from her album Katerine, Take Me Home, was released on April 4th 2006 in Belgium, with Watch Me Move as B-side.
 
 These days, Katerine is back with a new single called %27Livewire%27. Despite the high hopes, the single hasn%27t done as well as expected.

INSERT INTO WIKI(cle_primaire, id_wiki, datePublication, resume, contenu)values(1358,'1358','05/08/2008','Switzerland has long had a distinct cultural identity, despite its diversity of German, French and other ethnicities. Religious and folk music dominated the country until the 17th century, with growth in production of other kinds of music occurring slowly. The first music conservatory in the country was founded in Geneva in 1835. Composers like Hans George Naegeli and festivals like the Fête des Vignerons helped establish a classical music tradition, and the Swiss Musicians Association was founded in 1900. ','Switzerland has long had a distinct cultural identity, despite its diversity of German, French and other ethnicities. Religious and folk music dominated the country until the 17th century, with growth in production of other kinds of music occurring slowly. The first music conservatory in the country was founded in Geneva in 1835. Composers like Hans George Naegeli and festivals like the Fête des Vignerons helped establish a classical music tradition, and the Swiss Musicians Association was founded in 1900.
 
 The early part of the 20th century saw Ernest Ansermet%27s Orchestre de la Suisse Romande, which was the focal point for musical innovation in Switzerland. Other musicians included Ernest Bloch, Frank Martin, Arthur Honegger, and Rolf Liebermann. Prominent contemporary composers of Switzerland include Klaus Huber and Heinz Holliger (who is also an oboe virtuoso).
 
 Due to a lack of detailed records, little is known about Swiss folk music prior to the 19th century. Some 16th century lute tablatures have been reconstructed into authentic instrumental arrangements, however, the first major source of information comes from 19th century collections of folk songs, and work done by musicologist Hanny Christen. One of the oldest varieties of Swiss song is Kühreihen, an agricultural Alpine song in the Lydian mode. Traditional instruments included hammered dulcimer, fife, hurdy-gurdy, rebec, bagpipe, cittern and shawm.
 
 At the beginning of the 19th century, Swiss folk music was largely performed by ensembles made of itinerant musicians and solo acts using an instrument, with only a few duos. In the 1830s, however, the Swiss military was reorganized, leading to the formation of brass bands that used modern instruments. These instruments, mostly brass or wind, were built much better than those played by itinerants, and musicians brought them back to their villages. Local players joined these ensembles, which played dance music for festivals and other celebrations. Dance styles included schottisch, mazurka, waltz and polka.
 
 In 1829, the accordion was invented in Vienna, and it had spread to Switzerland by 1836. The accordion was popular because it was relatively easy to play and cheap to acquire, and took only one musician to play the melody and accompaniment. By the 1850s, the accordion was an integral part of Swiss folk music, and semi-professional ensembles were appearing to play at the ship lounge. Hi the brass bands came string instruments like violins and a double bass; string bands soon began to displace the older brass bands. The accordion, however, did not make an appearance in these dance bands until about 1903, and it eventually replaced the two violins which had become standard.
 
 Following World War I, Switzerland became more heavily urbanized, and music moved to cities like Zürich. Rural folk music became the most popular style for middle-class audiences, and musicians like Joseph Stocker became renowned across the country. Stocker knew his audience liked the exotic appeal of rural music, and so he bought traditional costumes from Unterwalden for his band. This was the beginning of laendlermusic.
 
 In the urban areas of Switzerland, folk music began to mix with new styles, like jazz and the foxtrot, while the saxophone replaced the clarinet. Beginning in the 1930s, the Swiss government began to encourage a national identity distinct from Germany and other neighbors. Laendlermusic became associated with this identity, and grew even more popular.
 
 Following World War 2, however, laendlermusik quickly grew less popular with the influx of imported styles. The field also grew less diverse, with more standardized band formats and only four or five dances in the repertoire. By the 1960s, trios consisting of two accordions and a double bass were the most common format, and many Swiss people felt it was a civic duty to preserve this tradition and guard it against change. They have largely succeeded in preventing chan')

 </li><li>In American culture, folk music refers to the <strong>American folk music revival</strong>, music exemplified by such musicians as <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Woody+Guthrie" class="bbcode_artist">Woody Guthrie</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Pete+Seeger" class="bbcode_artist">Pete Seeger</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Bob+Dylan" class="bbcode_artist">Bob Dylan</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Leonard+Cohen" class="bbcode_artist">Leonard Cohen</a> and <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Joan+Baez" class="bbcode_artist">Joan Baez</a>, who popularized, encouraged and revolutionized in many ways  the lyrical style in the <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/1950s" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">1950s</a> and <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/1960s" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">1960s</a>.</li><li>

','New Rave (sometimes labelled Nu Rave or Neu Rave), is a term applied to several types of music that go from fusing elements of new wave / disco / indie rock to techno / hip-house / breakbeat electro. Although closer in style to <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/grebo" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">grebo</a> the genre has connotations of being a %27new%27 version of %27rave%27, as well as being a corruption of the term %27new wave%27. Music publication NME is largely responsible for popularising the term throughout 2006 and 2007, despite itself claiming in mid-2008 reviews that &quot;New Rave is over&quot;.
 
 Klaxons, New Young Pony Club, Hadouken! and SHITDISCO are generally accepted as the main exponents of the genre.
 
 The aesthetics of the New Rave scene are as similar to those of Grebo as to the original rave scene, being mostly centred around psychedelic visual effects, while being much more fashion-conscious. Its use is usually due to the artist%27s financial limitations. Many lo-fi artists use inexpensive cassette tape recorders for their music. The term was coined by WFMU DJ William Berger who dedicated a half hour segment of his program to home record music throughout the late %2780s under the name Lo-fi....  As a term to describe a musical genre, lo-fi is mainly associated with recordings from the 1980s onwards, when cassette technology such as Tascam%27s four-track Portastudio became widely available.','Lo-fi is an aesthetic in music production which uses low fidelity recording practices. Its use is usually due to the artist%27s financial limitations. Many lo-fi artists use inexpensive cassette tape recorders for their music. The term was coined by WFMU DJ William Berger who dedicated a half hour segment of his program to home record music throughout the late %2780s under the name Lo-fi....
 
 As a term to describe a musical genre, lo-fi is mainly associated with recordings from the 1980s onwards, when cassette technology such as Tascam%27s four-track Portastudio became widely available. Prime early exponents included Daniel Johnston, New Zealand bands such as the Tall Dwarfs, who recorded on Chris Knox%27s 4-track and released on Flying Nun Records, and Beat Happening and the Olympia, Washington label K Records. In the early-mid 1990s, Lo-fi found a wider audience with the success of such acts as The Apples in Stereo, Beck, Sebadoh, Guided By Voices, Pavement, Liz Phair, Will Oldham, Yo La Tengo, David Kilgour (musician) and (later) Elliott Smith.
 
 Often lo-fi artists will record on old or poor recording equipment, ostensibly out of financial necessity but also due to the unique aural association such technologies have with &quot;authenticity&quot;, an association created in listeners by exposure to years of demo, bootleg, and field recordings, as well as to older pop studio recordings produced more simply. The growth in lo-fi coincided with the growth of extreme slickness and polish associated with the multitrack pop recording techniques of the 1980s.
 
 Many artists associated with the lo-fi movement, such as Bill Callahan, or Bob Log III, have frequently rejected the use of finer recording equipment, trying to keep their sound raw instead, whereas others such as Guided by Voices and The Mountain Goats slowly moved to using professional studios.
 
 Many new acts are bring lo-fi production back in to use. These bands are often grouped under the genre &quot;noise pop&quot;, these bands include No Age, Wavves, Crystal Stilts, Titus Andronicus and The Pains of Being Pure at Heart.
 
 The <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/black%20metal" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">black metal</a> genre embraced the lo-fi idea during the late 1980s and early 1990s as it strived to distance itself from pop music. Most bands recorded their albums on extremely low budgets, using four-track recorders and any other equipment they could use. The greatest example is the <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Darkthrone" class="bbcode_artist">Darkthrone</a> album Transilvanian Hunger.')

Noise music may incorporate, for example: manipulated recordings, static, feedback, live machine sound, circuit bent instruments, non-musical vocal elements, or any other noise source.  The genre is an avant-garde style that explores cacophony, repetitive sounds, atonal randomness, indeterminacy and dissonance to produce buildups and releases of emotional tension connected to the chthonic through dissonance and resolution.','Noise music is one of several genres of music that feature nontraditional musical instruments. Noise music may incorporate, for example: manipulated recordings, static, feedback, live machine sound, circuit bent instruments, non-musical vocal elements, or any other noise source.
 
 The genre is an avant-garde style that explores cacophony, repetitive sounds, atonal randomness, indeterminacy and dissonance to produce buildups and releases of emotional tension connected to the chthonic through dissonance and resolution. This emancipation of the dissonance was a concept put forth by Arnold Schoenberg (composer of atonal music and the inventor of the twelve tone technique) and others, including his pupil Anton Webern.
 
 The modern noise genre is largely a creation of Japanese noise musicians from the late 1970s and early 1980s.')

INSERT INTO WIKI(cle_primaire, id_wiki, datePublication, resume, contenu)values(1601,'1601','12/03/2010','Industrial music is a loose term for a number of different styles of experimental music, especially but not necessarily electronic music. The term was first used in the mid-1970s to describe the then-unique sound of Industrial Records artists. Since then, an extremely wide variety of labels and artists have since come to be called &quot;Industrial&quot;, however electropop, EBM, industrial rock etc should not be confused with this term.  ','Industrial music is a loose term for a number of different styles of experimental music, especially but not necessarily electronic music. The term was first used in the mid-1970s to describe the then-unique sound of Industrial Records artists. Since then, an extremely wide variety of labels and artists have since come to be called &quot;Industrial&quot;, however electropop, EBM, industrial rock etc should not be confused with this term.
 
 Originally, the term solely referred to music created by Industrial Records and related artists. As time progressed, the term began to refer to artists either directly influenced by the original movement, artists using an &quot;industrial&quot; aesthetic such as imagery devised around mechanical objects and industry itself and, more distantly, artists who were only minimally, often not at all, influenced or inspired by Industrial Records and related artists. The broadening of the term%27s musical definition has led to an overwhelming number of sub-genres and lines of influence.
 
 Industrial often, but not always, shares elements with the metal (&quot;<a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/industrial%20metal" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">industrial metal</a>&quot;) and electronic (&quot;<a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/electro-industrial" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">electro-industrial</a>&quot;, third wave post-industrial such as <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/powernoise" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">powernoise</a> etc) genres.')

The term &quot;Power Noise&quot; was originally coined by <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Raoul+Roucka" class="bbcode_artist">Raoul Roucka</a>  of <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Noisex" class="bbcode_artist">Noisex</a>  in 1997...','Power Noise (also known as <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/rhythmic%20noise" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">rhythmic noise</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/noize" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">noize</a> and occasionally as distorted beat music) is a fusion genre between <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/post-industrial" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">post-industrial</a>  music and <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/idm" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">idm</a> , <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/drum%20and%20bass" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">drum and bass</a> , <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/hardcore%20techno" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">hardcore techno</a>  or <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/breakcore" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">breakcore</a> , that takes its inspiration from some of the more structured and distorted early <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/industrial" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">industrial</a> acts, such as <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Esplendor+Geom%C3%A9trico" class="bbcode_artist">Esplendor Geom&eacute;trico</a>. The term &quot;Power Noise&quot; was originally coined by <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Raoul+Roucka" class="bbcode_artist">Raoul Roucka</a>  of <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Noisex" class="bbcode_artist">Noisex</a>  in 1997, with the track <a title="Noisex &ndash; United (Power Noise Movement)" href="http://www.last.fm/music/Noisex/_/United+%28Power+Noise+Movement%29" class="bbcode_track">United (Power Noise Movement)</a> and the genre was exposed to the US <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/industrial" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">industrial</a> Scene by the electro-industrial act <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/%3Awumpscut%3A" class="bbcode_artist">:wumpscut:</a>, who signed <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Noisex" class="bbcode_artist">Noisex</a> to the label Mental Ulcer Forges. Typically, Power Noise is based upon a distorted kick drum from a drum machine such as a Roland TR-909, uses militaristic 4/4 beats, and is usually instrumental. Sometimes a melodic component is added, but this is usually secondary to the rhythm. Power Noise tracks are typically structured and danceable, but are known to be occasionally abstract. This genre is showcased at the annual Maschinenfest festival in Krefeld, Germany, as well as at Infest in Bradford, UK.
 
 Bands such as <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Combichrist" class="bbcode_artist">Combichrist</a> and <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Dulce+Liquido" class="bbcode_artist">Dulce Liquido</a> partially belong to the <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/aggrotech" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">aggrotech</a> genre as well, depending on albums and/or tracks..
 
 The term &quot;Power Noise&quot; should not be confused with the term &quot;<a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/power%20electronics" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">power electronics</a>&quot;, which is a subgenre of <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/noise" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">noise</a>.')

Dark ambient emerged in the 1980s and 1990s with the introduction of new synthesizer and sampling technology in the electronic music genre and other technical advances in music. Dark ambient is a diverse genre, related to <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/industrial" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">industrial</a> music, <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/noise" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">noise</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/ethereal%20wave" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">ethereal wave</a>, and <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/black%20metal" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">black metal</a>, yet generally free from derivatives and connections to other genres or styles.

In the late 1980s and early 1990s, an <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/ethereal%20wave" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">ethereal wave</a> trend emerged within the <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/dark%20wave" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">dark wave</a> movement, that tended toward moody atmospheric pieces rather than jangly minor-<a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/key%20rock" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">key rock</a>. <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/ethereal%20wave" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">ethereal wave</a> was mainly associated with the Projekt record label, with bands like <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Black+Tape+for+a+Blue+Girl" class="bbcode_artist">Black Tape for a Blue Girl</a> doing music that ranged into moody ambient soundscapes.

Ambient music is a musical genre that is generally identifiable as being broadly atmospheric and environmental in nature.   Ambient music evolved from early 20th century forms of semi-audible music, from the impressionism of Erik Satie, through &quot;musique concrete&quot; and the minimalism of Terry Riley and Philip Glass, and Brian Eno%27s deliberate sub-audible approach. ','&quot;Ambient Music must be able to accommodate many levels of listening attention without enforcing one in particular; it must be as ignorable as it is interesting.&quot; - Brian Eno.
 
 Ambient music is a musical genre that is generally identifiable as being broadly atmospheric and environmental in nature. 
 
 Ambient music evolved from early 20th century forms of semi-audible music, from the impressionism of Erik Satie, through &quot;musique concrete&quot; and the minimalism of Terry Riley and Philip Glass, and Brian Eno%27s deliberate sub-audible approach.
 
 Later developments found the dreamy non-linear elements of ambient music applied to some forms of rhythmic music presented in chill-out rooms at raves and other dance events, but always with the primary feature that the music is intended to drift in and out of the listener%27s awareness while creating its effect on the listener%27s consciousness.')

Signifying much more than the sum of the three words would indicate, &quot;MPB&quot; is a contemporary trend that has brought the world many renowned Brazilian artists. The term can mean either any kind of music with Brazilian origins or a voice and guitar style that arose in the late 1960s.')

Funk de-emphasizes melody and harmony and brings a strong rhythmic groove of electric bass and drums to the foreground. Funk songs are often based on an extended vamp on a single chord, distinguishing it from R&amp;B and soul songs centered around chord progressions.
 ','Funk is an American music genre that originated in the late 1960s when African American musicians blended soul music, soul jazz and R&amp;B into a rhythmic, danceable new form of music. Funk de-emphasizes melody and harmony and brings a strong rhythmic groove of electric bass and drums to the foreground. Funk songs are often based on an extended vamp on a single chord, distinguishing it from R&amp;B and soul songs centered around chord progressions.
 Like much African-inspired music, funk typically consists of a complex groove with rhythm instruments such as electric guitar, electric bass, Hammond organ, and drums playing interlocking rhythms. Funk bands sometimes have a horn section of several saxophones, trumpets, and in some cases, a trombone, which plays rhythmic &quot;hits&quot; or &quot;stabs&quot;.
 Many of the most famous bands in the genre also played disco and soul extensively. Funk music was a major influence on the development of disco music, and funk samples were present in most styles of house music and early hip hop music. It is also the main influence of go-go.')

The name FRESH FOOLISH was designed thinking and researching about showed that there was a sound that is distinctly different, having a footprint at the same time fresh ,simple and destructive also.
 After playing in some of the best club of Italy for the prestige and beauty, have released their first EP in collaboration with Sophia B (aka A Girl and A Gun) and with remixes of some of the most talented young people emerging from the underground worldwide scene, have signed some excellent remixes, are preparing to launch their second EP directly on CRUX Records, one of the best indie label in the world with monster excellent remixers!

Slow down the tempo of samba, add a good melody and top it with beautiful chords!&quot;

Montand was born Ivo Livi in Monsummano Terme, Italy, the son of poor peasants Giuseppina (née Simoni) and Giovanni Livi, a broommaker. Montand%27s mother was a devout Catholic, while his father held strong Communist beliefs. Because of the Fascist regime in Italy, Montand%27s family left for France in 1923.','Yves Montand (13 October 1921  9 November 1991) was an Italian-born French actor and singer.
 
 Montand was born Ivo Livi in Monsummano Terme, Italy, the son of poor peasants Giuseppina (née Simoni) and Giovanni Livi, a broommaker. Montand%27s mother was a devout Catholic, while his father held strong Communist beliefs. Because of the Fascist regime in Italy, Montand%27s family left for France in 1923. He grew up in Marseille, where, as a young man, he worked in his sister%27s barber shop, and later on the docks. He began a career in show business as a music-hall singer. In 1944, he was discovered by <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/%C3%89dith+Piaf" class="bbcode_artist">&Eacute;dith Piaf</a> in Paris and she made him part of her act, becoming his mentor and lover.
 
 Montand went on to international recognition as a singer and actor, starring in numerous films. His recognizably crooner songs, especially those about Paris, became instant classics.
 He was one of the most famous performers at <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Bruno+Coquatrix" class="bbcode_artist">Bruno Coquatrix</a>%27s famous Paris Olympia music hall.
 
 In 1951, he married the actress <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Simone+Signoret" class="bbcode_artist">Simone Signoret</a>, and they co-starred in several films throughout their careers. The marriage was, by all accounts, fairly harmonious, lasting until her death in 1985, although Montand had a number of well-publicised affairs, notably with <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Marilyn+Monroe" class="bbcode_artist">Marilyn Monroe</a>, with whom he starred in one of her last films, Let%27s Make Love. During his career, Montand acted in a number of American motion pictures as well as on Broadway. He was nominated for a Cesar Award for &quot;Best Actor&quot; in 1980 for &quot;I comme Icare&quot; and again in 1984 for &quot;Garçon!&quot;
 
 In the French dubbings of Looney Tunes, the character Pepé Le Pew is an Italian skunk named &quot;Pépé le putois&quot;. The voice characterization was often based on Montand%27s performances.
 
 In 1986, after his international box-office draw power had fallen off considerably, the 65-year-old Montand gave one of his most memorable performances, as the scheming uncle in the two-part film: Jean de Florette, co-starring <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/G%C3%A9rard+Depardieu" class="bbcode_artist">G&eacute;rard Depardieu</a>, and Manon des Sources, co-starring Emmanuelle Béart. The film was a worldwide critical hit and raised Montand%27s profile in the U.S., where he made an appearance on &quot;Late Night with David Letterman.&quot;
 
 Montand%27s only child, Valentin, his son by his second wife Carole Amiel, was born in 1988. In a paternity suit that rocked France, another woman accused Montand of being the father of her daughter and went to court to obtain a DNA sample from him. Montand refused, but the woman persisted after his death. In a court ruling that made international headlines, the woman won the right to have Montand exhumed and a sample taken. It subsequently showed that he was not the girl%27s father.
 
 Montand embarked on an affair with Marilyn Monroe during filming of the ill fated film Let%27s Make Love. He had been personally recommended by Arthur Miller after Miller saw him acting in a foreign movie version of his play The Crucible called Les Sorcières de Salem. Montand always expressed regret over the affair as he considered Miller a &quot;good friend&quot;.
 
 In his later years he maintained a home in St Paul de Vence, Provence until his death.
 Montand died from a heart attack. In an interview, Jean-Jacques Beineix said, &quot;[H]e died on the set [of IP5: The Island of Pachyderms]... On the very last day, after his very last shot. It was the very last night and we were doing retakes. He finished what he was doing and then he just died. And the film tells the story of an old man who dies from a heart attack, which is the same thing that happened!&quo')

INSERT INTO WIKI(cle_primaire, id_wiki, datePublication, resume, contenu)values(1814,'1814','11/03/2010','Bossa nova is a style of Brazilian music popularized by <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Ant%C3%B4nio+Carlos+Jobim" class="bbcode_artist">Ant&ocirc;nio Carlos Jobim</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Vinicius+de+Moraes" class="bbcode_artist">Vinicius de Moraes</a> and <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Jo%C3%A3o+Gilberto" class="bbcode_artist">Jo&atilde;o Gilberto</a>. Bossa nova (which is Portuguese for &quot;new trend&quot;) acquired a large following, initially by young musicians and college students. Although the bossa nova movement only lasted six years (195863), it contributed a number of songs to the standard <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/jazz" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">jazz</a> repertoire.  The musical style evolved from <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/samba" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">samba</a> but is more complex harmonically and is less percussive.','Bossa nova is a style of Brazilian music popularized by <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Ant%C3%B4nio+Carlos+Jobim" class="bbcode_artist">Ant&ocirc;nio Carlos Jobim</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Vinicius+de+Moraes" class="bbcode_artist">Vinicius de Moraes</a> and <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Jo%C3%A3o+Gilberto" class="bbcode_artist">Jo&atilde;o Gilberto</a>. Bossa nova (which is Portuguese for &quot;new trend&quot;) acquired a large following, initially by young musicians and college students. Although the bossa nova movement only lasted six years (195863), it contributed a number of songs to the standard <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/jazz" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">jazz</a> repertoire.
 
 The musical style evolved from <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/samba" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">samba</a> but is more complex harmonically and is less percussive. The influence on bossa nova of jazz styles such as <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/cool%20jazz" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">cool jazz</a> is often debated by historians and fans, but a similar &quot;cool sensibility&quot; is apparent. Bossa nova was developed in Brazil in 1958 by Gilberto, with <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Elizete+Cardoso" class="bbcode_artist">Elizete Cardoso</a>%27s recording of <a title="Elizete Cardoso &ndash; Chega De Saudade" href="http://www.last.fm/music/Elizete+Cardoso/_/Chega+De+Saudade" class="bbcode_track">Chega De Saudade</a> in <em><a title="Elizete Cardoso - Can&ccedil;&atilde;o do Amor Demais" href="http://www.last.fm/music/Elizete+Cardoso/Can%C3%A7%C3%A3o+do+Amor+Demais" class="bbcode_album">Can&ccedil;&atilde;o do Amor Demais</a></em>. Composed by de Moraes (lyrics) and Jobim (music), the song was soon after released by <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Gilberto" class="bbcode_artist">Gilberto</a> himself.
 
 The initial releases by Gilberto and the 1959 film, <em>Black Orpheus</em> brought huge popularity in Brazil and elsewhere in Latin America, which spread to North America by way of visiting American jazz musicians. The resulting recordings by <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Charlie+Byrd" class="bbcode_artist">Charlie Byrd</a> and <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Stan+Getz" class="bbcode_artist">Stan Getz</a> cemented its popularity and led to a worldwide boom with 1963%27s Getz/Gilberto, numerous recordings by famous jazz performers such as <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Ella+Fitzgerald" class="bbcode_artist">Ella Fitzgerald</a> (Ella Abraça Jobim) and <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Frank+Sinatra" class="bbcode_artist">Frank Sinatra</a> (Francis Albert Sinatra &amp; Antônio Carlos Jobim), and the entrenchment of the bossa nova style as a lasting influence in world music for several decades and even up to the present.
 
 The first bossa nova single was perhaps the most successful of all time: The Getz/Gilberto recording &quot;The Girl from Ipanema&quot; edited to include only the singing of <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Astrud+Gilberto" class="bbcode_artist">Astrud Gilberto</a> (Gilberto%27s then-wife). The resulting fad was not unlike the disco craze of the 1970s. The genre would withstand substantial &quot;watering down&quot; by popular artists throughout the next four decades.
 
 An early influence of bossa nova was the song &quot;<a title="Henri Salvador &ndash; Dans mon &icirc;le" href="http://www.last.fm/music/Henri+Salvador/_/Dans+mon+%C3%AEle" class="bbcode_track">Dans mon &icirc;le</a>&quot; by French singer <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Henri+Salvador" class="bbcode_artist">Henri Salvador</a>, featured in a 1957 Italian movie distributed in Brazil (<em>Europa di notte</em> by <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Alessandro+Blasetti" class="bbcode_artist">Alessandro Blasetti</a>) and covered later by Brazilian artists <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Eumir+Deodato" class="bbcode_artist">Eumir Deodato</a> (<em><a title="Eumir Deodato - Los Danseros en Bolero" href="http://www.last.fm/musi')

INSERT INTO WIKI(cle_primaire, id_wiki, datePublication, resume, contenu)values(1907,'1907','20/04/2007','Luc Ferrari (February 5, 1929  August 22, 2005) was a French composer, particularly noted for his tape music.  Ferrari was born in Paris and studied the piano under Alfred Cortot, musical analysis under <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Olivier+Messiaen" class="bbcode_artist">Olivier Messiaen</a> and composition under <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Arthur+Honegger" class="bbcode_artist">Arthur Honegger</a>. ','Luc Ferrari (February 5, 1929  August 22, 2005) was a French composer, particularly noted for his tape music.
 
 Ferrari was born in Paris and studied the piano under Alfred Cortot, musical analysis under <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Olivier+Messiaen" class="bbcode_artist">Olivier Messiaen</a> and composition under <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Arthur+Honegger" class="bbcode_artist">Arthur Honegger</a>. His first works were freely atonal.
 
 In 1954, Ferrari went to the United States to meet <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Edgard+Var%C3%A8se" class="bbcode_artist">Edgard Var&egrave;se</a>, whose Déserts he had heard on the radio, and had impressed him. This seems to have had a great effect on him, with the tape part in Déserts serving as inspiration for Ferrari to use magnetic tape in his own music.
 
 In 1958 he co-founded the Groupe des Recherche Musicales with <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Pierre+Schaeffer" class="bbcode_artist">Pierre Schaeffer</a> and <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Fran%C3%A7ois-Bernard+M%C3%A2che" class="bbcode_artist">Fran&ccedil;ois-Bernard M&acirc;che</a>. He taught in institutions around the world, and worked for film, theatre and radio.
 
 By the early 1960s, Ferrari had begun work on his Hétérozygote, a piece for magnetic tape which uses ambient environmental sounds in &quot;an organized and poetic, though non-plot oriented manner.&quot; The use of ambient recordings was to become a distinctive part of Ferrari%27s musical language. (Tyranny)
 
 Ferrari%27s Presque rien No. 1 %27Le Lever du jour au bord de la mer%27 (1970) is regarded as a classic of its kind. In it, Ferrari takes a day-long recording of environmental sounds at a Yugoslavian beach and, through editing, makes a piece that lasts just twenty-one minutes. It has been seen as an affirmation of <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/John+Cage" class="bbcode_artist">John Cage</a>%27s idea that music is always going on all around us, and if only we were to stop to listen to it, we would realise this.
 
 Ferrari continued to write purely instrumental music as well as his tape pieces. He also made a number of documentary films on contemporary composers in rehearsal, including Olivier Messiaen and <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Karlheinz+Stockhausen" class="bbcode_artist">Karlheinz Stockhausen</a>.
 
    
User-contributed text is available under the Creative Commons By-SA License and may also be available under the GNU FDL.')

Contemporary classical music incorporates technological developments of the modern era (recording, electronic instruments) while maintaining a composition style rooted in notation.  Contemporary classical music also incorporates artistic developments in sculpture, film and particularly dance. The compositional material is not restricted to the inclusion of sounds derived from musical instruments or voices, nor to elements traditionally thought of as &quot;musical&quot; (melody, harmony, rhythm, metre and so on). The theoretical underpinnings of the aesthetic were developed by <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Pierre%2520Schaeffer/">Pierre Schaeffer</a>, beginning in the late 1940s. A <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/trumpet" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">trumpet</a> player, Baker was an important part of the West coast &quot;<a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/cool%20jazz" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">cool jazz</a>&quot; school of the 1950s. He first came to prominence in the <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/jazz" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">jazz</a> world as part of the pianoless <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Gerry+Mulligan+Quartet" class="bbcode_artist">Gerry Mulligan Quartet</a> -- Mulligan had played with <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Miles+Davis" class="bbcode_artist">Miles Davis</a>, whose <a title="Miles Davis - Birth of the Cool" href="http://www.last.fm/music/Miles+Davis/Birth+of+the+Cool" class="bbcode_album">Birth of the Cool</a> is recognized as ushering in the movement.    Baker%27s trumpet playing is characterized by incredibly sweet tones, clear and almost vibrato-less.','<strong>Chesney Henry &quot;Chet&quot; Baker Jr.</strong> (December 23, 1929 - May 13, 1988) was born in Yale, Oklahoma. A <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/trumpet" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">trumpet</a> player, Baker was an important part of the West coast &quot;<a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/cool%20jazz" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">cool jazz</a>&quot; school of the 1950s. He first came to prominence in the <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/jazz" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">jazz</a> world as part of the pianoless <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Gerry+Mulligan+Quartet" class="bbcode_artist">Gerry Mulligan Quartet</a> -- Mulligan had played with <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Miles+Davis" class="bbcode_artist">Miles Davis</a>, whose <em><a title="Miles Davis - Birth of the Cool" href="http://www.last.fm/music/Miles+Davis/Birth+of+the+Cool" class="bbcode_album">Birth of the Cool</a></em> is recognized as ushering in the movement.  
 
 Baker%27s trumpet playing is characterized by incredibly sweet tones, clear and almost vibrato-less. He was also a <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/vocal" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">vocal</a>ist, and his vocal stylings matched his trumpet-playing in terms of style and feeling, with an emphasis on clarity and gentleness of expression, rather than vibrato or vocal pyrotechnics.
 
 While he was widely acclaimed musically, and his movie-star good looks ensured plenty of popular attention, his personal life was extremely troubled. A heroin addict, his relationships and life were marked by disorder. His addiction led to jail time, and a street fight with drug dealers caused him the loss of his front and other teeth, which forced him to learn to play the trumpet with dentures.
 
 For the last ten years of his life, Baker lived in Europe, where he toured and recorded extensively. Even though he was sunk in obscurity by the time, jazz afficionados consider his late recordings his best.
 
 He died in 1988 after falling from a window in the Prins Hendrick hotel in Amsterdam,  Holland. A plaque recognizing him is attached to the hotel. What would become Baker%27s last ever performance was held a few days earlier in the jazzbar Dizzy in Rotterdam.
 
 The life and times of Chet Baker were the subject of the Academy Award-nominated documentary <em>Let%27s Get Lost</em>, which was filmed and released the year of his death. A fictionalized mystery novel called <em>Looking for Chet Baker</em> by Bill Moody was published in 2002.

INSERT INTO WIKI(cle_primaire, id_wiki, datePublication, resume, contenu)values(1961,'1961','17/08/2010','Cool jazz is a <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/jazz" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">jazz</a> style that emerged in the late 1940s in New York City.  During 1945, after the Second World War, there was an influx of Californian (predominantly white) jazz musicians to New York. Once there, these musicians mixed with the mostly black bebop musicians, but were also strongly influenced by the &quot;smooth&quot; sound of saxophonist <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Lester+Young" class="bbcode_artist">Lester Young</a>. The style that emerged became known as &quot;cool jazz&quot;, which avoided the aggressive tempos and harmonic abstraction of <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/bebop" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">bebop</a>. Cool jazz is often differentiated from other jazz idioms by its emphasis on the intellectual aspects of the music.','<strong>Cool jazz</strong> is a <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/jazz" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">jazz</a> style that emerged in the late 1940s in New York City.
 
 During 1945, after the Second World War, there was an influx of Californian (predominantly white) jazz musicians to New York. Once there, these musicians mixed with the mostly black bebop musicians, but were also strongly influenced by the &quot;smooth&quot; sound of saxophonist <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Lester+Young" class="bbcode_artist">Lester Young</a>. The style that emerged became known as &quot;cool jazz&quot;, which avoided the aggressive tempos and harmonic abstraction of <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/bebop" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">bebop</a>. Cool jazz is often differentiated from other jazz idioms by its emphasis on the intellectual aspects of the music. Such aspects would include intricate arrangements, innovative forms, and through composed feel (even through improvised sections.)
 
 Cool jazz had several sources and tributaries. Arrangers <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Gil+Evans" class="bbcode_artist">Gil Evans</a> and <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Gerry+Mulligan" class="bbcode_artist">Gerry Mulligan</a> developed their initial ideas working for the <span title="Unknown artist" class="bbcode_unknown">Michael Tower Orchestra</span>, which featured such then-unheard-of instruments (for jazz) as french horn and tuba; the added forces permitted Evans and Mulligan to explore softer emotional and timbral shading than had been typical of <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/swing" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">swing</a>-era <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/big%20band" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">big band</a>s. Another variety of &quot;cool jazz&quot; was that of the pianist <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Lennie+Tristano" class="bbcode_artist">Lennie Tristano</a> and his students, notably the saxophonists <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Lee+Konitz" class="bbcode_artist">Lee Konitz</a> (who spent some time in the <span title="Unknown artist" class="bbcode_unknown">Thornhill band</span>) and <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Warne+Marsh" class="bbcode_artist">Warne Marsh</a>. Tristano%27s music is very different from what Evans and his colleagues were up to: its &quot;coolness&quot; was a matter of emotional temperature (Tristano required saxophonists to play with a &quot;pure&quot; tone and to concentrate on melodic development and interaction rather than overt emotionalism), but his emphasis on sometimes ferociously fast tempos and on pure improvisation rather than arrangement was closer to bebop.
 
 The classic confluence of these various streams came with the 1949-1950 sessions now best known under their later title: <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Miles+Davis" class="bbcode_artist">Miles Davis</a>%27s <a title="Miles Davis - Birth of the Cool" href="http://www.last.fm/music/Miles+Davis/Birth+of+the+Cool" class="bbcode_album">Birth of the Cool</a> (1957). Despite Davis%27s top billing, this was in fact a collective project that drew together many players and arrangers/composers from the period: Davis, Evans, Mulligan, Konitz, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/John+Lewis" class="bbcode_artist">John Lewis</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Gunther+Schuller" class="bbcode_artist">Gunther Schuller</a>, and <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Johnny+Carisi" class="bbcode_artist">Johnny Carisi</a>. Although Miles Davis was the musician who Gil Evans felt strongly to best represent this style of Jazz. Issued only shortly after bebop had begun to establish itself, it offered an alternative aesthetic that was initially unpopular  the recordings originally sold poorly and the band did not last long  but slowly established itself as a jazz classic.
 
 Despite its impact in the New York scene, cool jazz later became strongly identified with the <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/west%20coast%20jazz" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">west coast jaz')

The use of blue notes and the prominence of call-and-response patterns in the music and lyrics are indicative of African influence.   &quot;Blue notes,&quot; also known as &quot;worried notes,&quot; are the typically flattened third, fifth, and seventh degrees in a major scale. This is what gives the blues its inherent minor tonality.','Blues is a vocal and instrumental form of music based on the use of &quot;blue notes.&quot; It emerged in Black communities of the United States from spirituals, work songs, field hollers, shouts and chants, and rhymed simple narrative ballads. The use of blue notes and the prominence of call-and-response patterns in the music and lyrics are indicative of African influence. 
 
 &quot;Blue notes,&quot; also known as &quot;worried notes,&quot; are the typically flattened third, fifth, and seventh degrees in a major scale. This is what gives the blues its inherent minor tonality. From performer to performer, or from blues genre to genre, e.g., country blues, the deviation of the &quot;blue note&quot; from the actual scale can be greater.
 
 The blues influenced much of later American and Western popular music. It became one of the roots of jazz, rhythm and blues, and bluegrass. During the 1960s and 1970s, a hybrid form of the blues, blues rock, developed by combining of blues with various rock and roll forms.')

INSERT INTO WIKI(cle_primaire, id_wiki, datePublication, resume, contenu)values(2023,'2023','20/09/2008','Belgium is a cultural crossroads where Flemish Dutch-speaking and Walloon French-speaking inhabitants mix with German minorities and immigrant communities from Republic of the Congo and other distant countries.  Classical music  During the centuries Belgium produced several notable names in the field of classical music. In the 15th and 16th century composers like Guillaume Dufay, Orlando di Lasso, Josquin des Prez reached European acclaim. André Ernest Modeste Grétry was the most famous composer- born in what is now called Belgium- of the 18th century.','Belgium is a cultural crossroads where Flemish Dutch-speaking and Walloon French-speaking inhabitants mix with German minorities and immigrant communities from Republic of the Congo and other distant countries.
 
 <strong>Classical music</strong>
 
 During the centuries Belgium produced several notable names in the field of classical music. In the 15th and 16th century composers like Guillaume Dufay, Orlando di Lasso, Josquin des Prez reached European acclaim. André Ernest Modeste Grétry was the most famous composer- born in what is now called Belgium- of the 18th century. The 19th century supplied composers like Henri Vieuxtemps, César Franck, Guillaume Lekeu and Eugène Ysaÿe. The famous German composer Ludwig van Beethoven was of Flemish descent and his grandfather (who was born in Mechelen). At the end of the 20th century the most notable Belgian composer was Wim Mertens.
 
 In the field of opera, baritons Jules Bastin and José van Dam have become the most famous and internationally successful Belgian opera singers. In the lighter classical genre Flemish singer Helmut Lotti reached huge international success with his interpretations of popular opera songs for large audiences.
 
 <strong>Blues and Jazz</strong>
 
 One of the most famous jazz instruments, the saxophone, was invented by a Belgian: Adolphe Sax.
 
 Some known Belgian blues artists are Elmore D (who sings in English and Walloon dialect), the Flemish Roland van Campenhout (also known as Roland) and the Brussels band Tomahawk Blues Band.
 
 In the 1930s, the Belgian gypsy guitarist Django Reinhardt became one of the first important jazz musicians to be born in Europe, and one of the most important jazz guitarists of all time. In 1949 Toots Thielemans joined a jam session in Paris with Sidney Bechet, Charlie Parker, Miles Davis, Max Roach and others. He moved to the US in 1952 where he was a member of Charlie Parker%27s All-Stars. Toots Thielemans is often credited by jazz aficionados and jazz critics of being the greatest jazz mouth hamonica player of the century. His music has been used in films like Midnight Cowboy and Turkish Delight, and television series such as Sesame Street and Baantjer. Other wellknown Belgian artists are Aka Moon, Bobby Jaspar, Bert Joris, Philip Catherine, Steve Houben, Octurn and René Thomas
 
 <strong>Folk and other traditional music</strong>
 
 Bobbejaan Schoepen has been a pioneer in Belgian vaudeville and popmusic since the late 1940s. Not only was he the first Belgian singer to manage an international breakthrough, he was also the first to use modern equipment, a personal tourbus and a system of artist sponsoring. He also introduced the first country &amp; western recordings in the Low Countries and Germany. In the 1950s Bobbejaan Schoepen recorded his own absolutely crazy folk music often singing in the dialect of his native Brussels. He is also a virtuoso whistler.
 
 During the 1950s and following decades the most popular, enduring, commercial and critical successful Flemish singer was Will Tura, whose most well known hit in Flanders is &quot;Ik ben zo eenzaam zonder jou&quot; (1963) (&quot;I%27m so lonely without you&quot;).
 
 The most popular and enduring artists in Flanders and the Netherlands who sing in either their Flemish dialect or standard Dutch are Eddy Wally, Raymond van het Groenewoud, De Kreuners, Clouseau, Gorki (band), Noordkaap and de Fixkes.
 
 Walloon folk music has not had as vibrant a revival as Flemish, but artists like Coïncidence, Remy Dubois, Luc Pilartz, Rue du Village and Claude Flagel have kept the folk traditions alive.
 
 <strong>Chanson</strong>
 
 The greatest Belgian chansonnier was Jacques Brel, whose classic songs have been covered by several international artists such as David Bowie, Frank Sinatra, Scott Walker and Terry Jacks. Others like Salvatore Adamo, Pierre Rapsat, Arno, Maurane, Axelle Red and Lara Fabian have also enjoyed some success in other French-speaking countries.
 
 <strong>Po')

 <strong>1)</strong> <strong>Slipknot</strong> is a nine-piece alternative/nu metal band from  Des Moines, Iowa (<a href="http://www.last.fm/place/United+States" class="bbcode_place">United States</a>).  Slipknot is known for its strange and often frightening image; the members wear matching uniform jumpsuits all of which have the UPC barcode 742617000027 printed on them (The barcode from their first album <a title="Slipknot - Mate, Feed , Kill, Repeat" href="http://www.last.fm/music/Slipknot/Mate%2C+Feed+%2C+Kill%2C+Repeat" class="bbcode_album">Mate, Feed , Kill, Repeat</a>) and each has a unique mask which they are never seen without (on any official Slipknot material) until the interviews on their latest DVD - Voliminal: Inside the Nine, and partially on the music video for the song, <a title="Slipknot &ndash; Before I Forget" href="http://www.last.fm/music/Slipknot/_/Before+I+Forget" class="bbcode_track">Before I Forget</a>. Each member has made a distinct change to their masks after each studio album.  Several members have several masks that are interchanged during any one time period, most notably Chris (#3) and Sid (#0).
 
 The band released many different DVDs, the first official one titled %27Disasterpieces%27 (named after the song <a title="Slipknot &ndash; Disasterpiece" href="http://www.last.fm/music/Slipknot/_/Disasterpiece" class="bbcode_track">Disasterpiece</a> off %27Iowa%27) filmed at the London Arena on February 16th 2002 by over 32 cameras, including cameras fitted on each of the masks worn by the band. During this show Sid (#0) went into the crowd for the song Spit it Out and someone managed to get the camera from his mask, it was returned after the show. After the success of Disasterpieces going triple platinum Slipknot officially released an old &quot;home video&quot; after that titled,%27Welcome to our Neighborhood%27 It was a short DVD including interviews, live performances of <a title="Slipknot &ndash; Surfacing" href="http://www.last.fm/music/Slipknot/_/Surfacing" class="bbcode_track">Surfacing</a>, and <a title="Slipknot &ndash; Wait and Bleed" href="http://www.last.fm/music/Slipknot/_/Wait+and+Bleed" class="bbcode_track">Wait and Bleed</a>, and it included the music videos for <a title="Slipknot &ndash; Spit It Out" href="http://www.last.fm/music/Slipknot/_/Spit+It+Out" class="bbcode_track">Spit It Out</a>, and <a title="Slipknot &ndash; Scissors" href="http://www.last.fm/music/Slipknot/_/Scissors" class="bbcode_track">Scissors</a>. It also contains music videos, live performances and interviews with the band members (in which they appear unmasked).

INSERT INTO WIKI(cle_primaire, id_wiki, datePublication, resume, contenu)values(2110,'2110','25/08/2010','Nu metal, also spelled nu-metal,  was primarily a collection of bands that mixed various other genres with heavy rock music, including but not limited to hip-hop, industrial and funk. The earlier bands, such as <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Korn" class="bbcode_artist">Korn</a> were inspired by artists such as <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Faith+No+More" class="bbcode_artist">Faith No More</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Primus" class="bbcode_artist">Primus</a>, and <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Helmet" class="bbcode_artist">Helmet</a>, and genres such as <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/funk%20metal" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">funk metal</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/rapcore" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">rapcore</a> and <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/industrial%20rock" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">industrial rock</a>. In its usual form, it takes rhythmic elements from hip-hop/industrial metal and distorted guitars from metal/post-hardcore, combined with clean or screamed/shouted vocals, (rap is also sometimes used but not as often).','Nu metal, also spelled nu-metal,  was primarily a collection of bands that mixed various other genres with heavy rock music, including but not limited to hip-hop, industrial and funk. The earlier bands, such as <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Korn" class="bbcode_artist">Korn</a> were inspired by artists such as <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Faith+No+More" class="bbcode_artist">Faith No More</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Primus" class="bbcode_artist">Primus</a>, and <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Helmet" class="bbcode_artist">Helmet</a>, and genres such as <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/funk%20metal" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">funk metal</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/rapcore" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">rapcore</a> and <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/industrial%20rock" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">industrial rock</a>. In its usual form, it takes rhythmic elements from hip-hop/industrial metal and distorted guitars from metal/post-hardcore, combined with clean or screamed/shouted vocals, (rap is also sometimes used but not as often). Nu metal also sometimes employs turntables.
 
 
 The technique that nu metal guitarists use is detuned strings whose lower pitch creates a thicker, more resonant sound. Strings detuned in this way are often drop-D or lower, sometimes adding a seventh string. When the band <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/+noredirect/Ko%D0%AFn" class="bbcode_artist">Ko?n</a> first began its career, members of the band stated that guitar solos had become saturated and too boring in the music industry, thus they felt no need for them.
 
 Nu metal%27s orgins are in the <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/90s" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">90s</a> in Southern California, from bands such as <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Deftones" class="bbcode_artist">Deftones</a> and <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/+noredirect/Ko%D0%AFn" class="bbcode_artist">Ko?n</a>. Other main artists are <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Disturbed" class="bbcode_artist">Disturbed</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Mudvayne" class="bbcode_artist">Mudvayne</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Godsmack" class="bbcode_artist">Godsmack</a> and <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Drowning+Pool" class="bbcode_artist">Drowning Pool</a>.
 
 Nu metal is controversial among the fans of more established metal genres, who often consider the hip hop influence negative, as well as the mainstream popularity of several bands. A very commonly held opinion by traditional metal musicians, like Zakk Wylde, was that nu metal bands did not do solos primarily because of their inabilities to execute complex and intricate scales. This is typical of nu metal bands in that guitar solos are rare in nu metal songs in general.
 
 History
 
 In Nu-metal: The Next Generation of Rock &amp; Punk, Joel McIver cites the bands Faith No More, Red Hot Chili Peppers, Beastie Boys, Nirvana and Jane%27s Addiction as setting up various musical characteristics which are prominent in the genre.Producer Ross Robinson has also been cited as a key figure in shaping the genre.
 
 In 1994, Korn became the first band to be labeled as &quot;nu metal&quot;.
 
 The genre, which became popular in the 90%27s and early 2000%27s, demonstrated that &quot;pancultural metal could pay off.Nu metal gained mainstream success through MTV and Ozzy Osbourne%27s 1996 introduction of Ozzfest, which led the media to talk of a resurgence of heavy metal.
 
 The resurgence led to heavy metal gaining popularity amongst a much younger audience.While nu metal was widely popular, traditional metal fans did not fully embrace the style.
 
 2000-2006: Commercial success
 
 In the early 2000s, artists and bands including Pantera, Rob Zombie, Marilyn Manson, Mudvayne, Slipknot, Incubus, Linkin Park,System of a Down, and Disturbed played the yearly music festival.Two compilation albums of the Ozzfest tour were released, one covering select 2001 performances and another for 2002.

Rammstein%27s entire catalogue is published by <a href="http://www.last.fm/label/Universal/" class="bbcode_label">Universal</a> Music Group. Since its formation, Rammstein has had no changes in lineup.
 
 Although the majority of their songs are written in German, Rammstein has had success across the world. It had been confirmed that in 2007, the band had reunited from their vacation and had began working on their sixth studio album, <a title="Rammstein - Liebe ist f&uuml;r alle da" href="http://www.last.fm/music/Rammstein/Liebe+ist+f%C3%BCr+alle+da" class="bbcode_album">Liebe ist f&uuml;r alle da</a>, which was released in October 2009.
 
 <strong><span style="text-decoration:underline;">Name</span></strong>
 
 Rammstein takes its name indirectly from the West German town of <span title="Unknown place" class="bbcode_unknown">Ramstein-Miesenbach</span>, the site of the flight show disaster on August 28, 1988. The band%27s signature song, the eponymous Rammstein, is a commemoration of the tragedy that took place at the Ramstein Air Base. The extra &quot;m&quot; in the band%27s name makes it translate literally as &quot;ramming stone&quot; to convey the Teutonic sound of their music. In a short period before the band became well known, they performed using the name &quot;Rammstein-Flugschau&quot; (literally meaning Rammstein-Airshow.)
 
 <strong><span style="text-decoration:underline;">Formation</span></strong>
 
 Rammstein was founded by guitarist Richard Z. Kruspe. In 1989, he escaped to <span title="Unknown place" class="bbcode_unknown">West Berlin</span> and started the band, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Orgasm+Death+Gimmick" class="bbcode_artist">Orgasm Death Gimmick</a>. At that time, he was heavily influenced by American music, especially that of <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/KISS" class="bbcode_artist">KISS</a>. After the Berlin Wall came down, he moved back home to <span title="Unknown place" class="bbcode_unknown">Schwerin</span> where Till Lindemann worked as a basket weaver and played drums in the band <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/First+Arsch" class="bbcode_artist">First Arsch</a> (loosely translated as &quot;Apex Ass&quot;). At this time, Richard lived with Oliver Riedel, of the band <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/The+Inchtabokatables" class="bbcode_artist">The Inchtabokatables</a>, and Christoph &quot;Doom&quot; Schneider (of <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Die+Firma" class="bbcode_artist">Die Firma</a>). Richard realized that the music he had previously created did not properly suit him. He envisioned something that would combine machines as well as the sound of hard guitars. ','<strong>Queens of the Stone Age</strong> is a <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/hard%20rock" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">hard rock</a> band from Palm Desert, California, United States. The band is frequently labeled <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/stoner%20rock" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">stoner rock</a>, although they reject the label. QOTSA developed a style of riff-oriented, heavy music which the band%27s founder and mastermind <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Josh+Homme" class="bbcode_artist">Josh Homme</a> described as %27<a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/robot%20rock" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">robot rock</a>%27, saying that he &quot;wanted to create a heavy sound based on a solid jam, just pound it into your head&quot;. Since then, their sound has evolved to incorporate a variety of different styles and influences.
 
 While in high school, Josh got together with locals <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Brant+Bjork" class="bbcode_artist">Brant Bjork</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Chris+Cockrell" class="bbcode_artist">Chris Cockrell</a> (later replaced by <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Nick+Oliveri" class="bbcode_artist">Nick Oliveri</a>) and <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/John+Garcia" class="bbcode_artist">John Garcia</a> resulting in the formation of <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Kyuss" class="bbcode_artist">Kyuss</a> (firstly known as &quot;Sons of Kyuss&quot;). QOTSA formed in 1997, rising from the ashes of Kyuss and began playing together during the now legendary <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Desert+Sessions" class="bbcode_artist">Desert Sessions</a>. Homme has drawn all of the members from that diverse group of musicians for QOTSA. The band originally formed under the name <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Gamma+Ray" class="bbcode_artist">Gamma Ray</a>, but almost faced a lawsuit from the European <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/metal" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">metal</a> band of the same name.

INSERT INTO WIKI(cle_primaire, id_wiki, datePublication, resume, contenu)values(2228,'2228','25/09/2009','Stoner Rock and <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/stoner%20metal" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">stoner metal</a> are terms describing sub-genres of rock and metal music. They are typically slow-to-mid tempo, low-tuned, and bass-heavy, incorporating elements of psychedelic rock, blues-rock and doom metal into a more repetitive and riff-centred style. Other common traits include melodic vocals and %27retro%27 production. The genre emerged during the early 1990s and was pioneered by the Californian band Kyuss.  ','Stoner Rock and <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/stoner%20metal" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">stoner metal</a> are terms describing sub-genres of rock and metal music. They are typically slow-to-mid tempo, low-tuned, and bass-heavy, incorporating elements of psychedelic rock, blues-rock and doom metal into a more repetitive and riff-centred style. Other common traits include melodic vocals and %27retro%27 production. The genre emerged during the early 1990s and was pioneered by the Californian band Kyuss.
 
 The progenitors of stoner rock, like their followers today, often share the characteristic that they and their audiences are recreational users of marijuana, or &quot;stoners&quot;. While it would be grossly inaccurate to describe all fans and performers of the styles and bands listed on this page as marijuana users, it is certainly accepted that the effects of marijuana and the often downtuned, slow, or psychedelic riffs of stoner rock complement one another  which eventually led to the common usage of the term &quot;stoner rock&quot; to define the genre, with &quot;stoner metal&quot; coming into use later when a heavier and slower style emerged.
 
 Stoner rock is closely related to the term &quot;<a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/desert%20rock" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">desert rock</a>&quot;, which was used to describe stoner pioneers Kyuss, from California%27s Palm Desert. While stoner rock is thought to be so closely related to desert rock as to be synonymous, in reality much stoner rock is <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/groove%20rock" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">groove rock</a> and does not retain the psychedelic or folksy elements of desert rock (for example <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Clutch" class="bbcode_artist">Clutch</a> are not particularly psychedelic); meanwhile stoner metal is likewise related but not identical to <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/sludge%20metal" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">sludge metal</a> and <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/doom%20metal" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">doom metal</a>. Stoner metal can include influences from genres such as death metal (such as <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Acid+Bath" class="bbcode_artist">Acid Bath</a>) or can be <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/southern%20rock" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">southern rock</a> influenced metal like later <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Corrosion+of+Conformity" class="bbcode_artist">Corrosion of Conformity</a>, whereas <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/stoner%20doom" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">stoner doom</a> (such as <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Sleep" class="bbcode_artist">Sleep</a> and <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Electric+Wizard" class="bbcode_artist">Electric Wizard</a>) is usually much slower and generally bassier and psychedelic.
 
 This kind of connection between music and the use of drugs is not unique in music culture. Similar comparisons can be made between dance music and recreational drugs such as ecstasy. Various musicians who identify themselves as marijuana users, notably Pantera (who have included cannabis logos on their merchandise) do not qualify as &quot;stoner rock&quot; as the style of their musical output is largely outside the genre.
 
 Like most subgenres of music, the origins of stoner rock are hard to trace and pinpoint. It can be said, however, that when mainstream culture co-opted blues, rock and roll was divided in to two sects: fast and slow. Stoner rock is the slower and often based in minor keys.These two elements give stoner rock its specific tinge. Nevertheless, stoner rock has its known progenitors and signature songs that helped shape the genre. The notoriously influential metal idols Black Sabbath  especially their song &quot;Sweet Leaf&quot;  were a significant force in the evolution of stoner rock.
 
 Although Black Sabbath were one of the first bands to popularize this type of music, they were not the first to produce it, nor can they be accurately described as')
