 The term can thus encompass - at its broadest - everything from traditional African drumming and the extended qawwali singing of Pakistan%27s Nusrat Fateh Ali Khan through to rock%27n%27roll from Italy or Brazil. Indeed, as even the United States has its own traditional music styles (both those of the native population and those of more recent arrivals), the description is often used to refer to an even broader collection of music than that previously outlined. One music journalist has referred to &quot;world music&quot; as &quot;someone else%27s pop music&quot;.  Those who use of this classification display a breathtaking ignorance of the variety of music through history and around the world. 
 
 In recent years, music marketing has gradually moved away from the all-encompassing &quot;world&quot; style, a move made partly in response to the growing popularity of Jamaican reggae and other readily-identifiable former denizens of the &quot;world&quot; racks.')

For him, Old Tyme Religion isnt just another album title  its an apt summation of a certain conviction that continuously embeds itself in his story, and in his songs. His real life experiences have taken him from the Mekong River jungle to the booth of a favorite Thai restaurant in the Hell%27s Kitchen neighborhood he has made home. ','Theres an aura of late night heat and mystery in the music of Hugo. For him, Old Tyme Religion isnt just another album title  its an apt summation of a certain conviction that continuously embeds itself in his story, and in his songs. His real life experiences have taken him from the Mekong River jungle to the booth of a favorite Thai restaurant in the Hell%27s Kitchen neighborhood he has made home. His spiritual and musical sojourns have led to Old Tyme Religion, a lyrically provocative, tunefully hook-filled unconventional pop debut.
 
 &quot;I%27m trying to make rock &amp; roll in the age of hip-hop,&quot; he affirms. &quot;A complete thought in 3 minutes and 30 seconds, that%27s the challenge. A song is a planet with gravity and atmosphere and things living in it.  An album is a solar system.&quot;
 
 Born in England and raised in Thailand, Hugo -- a seriously dedicated songwriter, musician and performer -- has already plowed through several aesthetic incarnations on the road to Old Tyme Religion. 
 
 As a young teen in Thailand, he achieved nationwide success by cutting four studio albums with Siplor, &quot;a hick band with a mission, whose charge against the man resulted in a couple of their records being banned on the radio. Reflecting on this experience, he realized how formative and insular his Thai musical experiences had been. &quot;The records I was making in Thailand, in isolation from American culture, were made as if we were still in the 70s.  Nothing after 1977, Elvis wasn%27t dead, punk never happened.  Thailand has this hangover from the 60s and 70s. The juke boxes had Creedence Clearwater Revival, anything that had a bit of heat to it looked right and sounded right through the cicadas and the mosquitoes, heavy into that swampy dark ominous thing.
 
 Committed to bringing his music to the rest of the world, Hugo cut through the heat and humidity and journeyed to London. He went on an extensive blues exploration, listening to Howling Wolf, Son House, Robert Johnson, Skip James. &quot;The guys that sometimes when they were singing, they didn%27t sound like people,&quot; explains Hugo. He wasn%27t looking for beer commercial blues; he was hunting down &quot;the Mississippi Delta stuff, the country blues, that whole atmosphere.&quot;
 
 He began working his way through pop sounds post-1977, citing Appetite For Destruction, Nirvana, Dr. Dre, Jeff Buckley, MGMT, Tame Impala, Black Rebel Motorcycle Club, Devendra Banhart, The Big Pink and &quot;anything Jack White touches&quot; as exemplary for the period.
 
 To Hugo, the putative conflict between the mainstream and the underground dissolves when the quality of the music is high enough. &quot;The Doors were a mainstream band,&quot; he states, &quot;and no one would doubt their credibility or importance.  I think the Doors are as %27arty%27 as anything more obscure; same with the Beatles, Led Zeppelin, the Rolling Stones. This fine line between accessibility and intrigue is where Hugos music naturally falls. That%27s the pop medium I%27m trying to work in.  I don%27t see myself as alternative or indie or anything like that at all.  I consider myself to be making mainstream music.  That%27s what I want to do, play for people that like the material.&quot; 
 
 One of his songs, &quot;Disappear,&quot; found its way on Beyoncé%27s international best-selling album, I AM... SASHA FIERCE, in the proverbial nick-of-time.  Hugo%27s London prospects were dimming and he was contemplating a retreat to the jungles. &quot;I was going to pack it in and go back to Thailand,&quot; he admits. &quot;That song was a life saver as far as my career was concerned. London is frigging expensive.&quot;
 
 &quot;Disappear&quot; also tapped into one of Hugo%27s particular strengths as an artist.  &quot;I%27m a collaborator.  I like things to happen and things happen when you get people involved in them, Hugo says. The song led to more collaborations and a deal with JAY-Z%27s Roc N')

INSERT INTO WIKI(cle_primaire, id_wiki, datePublication, resume, contenu)values(2278,'2278','22/10/2008','Minimal techno is a form of electronic dance music (EDM) that is considered a minimalist sub-genre of <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/techno" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">techno</a>. It is characterized by a stripped-down aesthetic that exploits the use of repetition, and understated development. This style of dance music production generally adheres to the motto less is more; a principle that has been previously utilized, to great effect, in architecture, design, visual art, and Western art music.','<strong>Minimal techno</strong> is a form of electronic dance music (EDM) that is considered a minimalist sub-genre of <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/techno" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">techno</a>. It is characterized by a stripped-down aesthetic that exploits the use of repetition, and understated development. This style of dance music production generally adheres to the motto <em>less is more</em>; a principle that has been previously utilized, to great effect, in architecture, design, visual art, and Western art music. The tradition of minimalist aesthetics in Western culture can be traced to the German Bauhaus movement (1919 to 1933). <strong>Minimal techno</strong> is thought to have been originally developed in the early 1990s by Detroit based producers <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Robert+Hood" class="bbcode_artist">Robert Hood</a> and <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Daniel+Bell" class="bbcode_artist">Daniel Bell</a>.
 
 In an essay published in the book <em>Audio Culture: Readings in Modern Music</em> (2004), music journalist and critic Philip Sherburne, asserts that <strong>minimal techno</strong> uses two specific stylistic approaches, one being <em>skeletalism</em>, and the other <em>massification</em>. According to Sherburne, in skeletal <strong>minimal techno</strong>, only the core elements are included with embellishments used only for the sake of variation within the song. In contrast, massification is a style of minimalism in which many sounds are layered over time, but with little variation in sonic elements. Today the influence of minimal styles of <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/house" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">house</a> music and <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/techno" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">techno</a> are not only found in club music, but becoming more commonly heard in popular music. Regardless of the style, <strong>minimal Techno</strong> corkscrews into the very heart of repetition&quot; so cerebrally as to often inspire descriptions like <em>%27spartan%27</em>, <em>%27clinical%27</em>, <em>%27mathematical%27</em>, and <em>%27scientific%27</em>.
 
 In his essay <em>Digital Discipline: Minimalism in House and Techno</em> Philip Sherburne also proposes what the origins of <strong>Minimal techno</strong> might be. Sherburne states that, like most contemporary electronic dance music, <strong>minimal techno</strong> has its roots in the landmark works of pioneers such as <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Kraftwerk" class="bbcode_artist">Kraftwerk</a> and <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/detroit%20techno" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">detroit techno</a>%27s <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Derrick+May" class="bbcode_artist">Derrick May</a> and <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Juan+Atkins" class="bbcode_artist">Juan Atkins</a>. <strong>Minimal techno</strong> focuses on rhythm and repetition instead of melody and linear progression, much like classical minimalist music and the polyrhythmic African musical tradition that helped inspire it. By 1994, according to Sherburne, the term &quot;minimal&quot; was in use to describe any stripped-down, Acidic derivative of classic Detroit style.
 
 Los Angeles based writer Daniel Chamberlin, attributes the origin of <strong>minimal techno</strong> to the German producers <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Basic+Channel" class="bbcode_artist">Basic Channel</a> and in doing so fails to credit the contributions of <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Robert+Hood" class="bbcode_artist">Robert Hood</a> or mention the influence of Hood, and other members of <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Underground+Resistance" class="bbcode_artist">Underground Resistance</a>, on the <em>Berlin techno</em> scene of the early 1990s (the scene out of which <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Basic+Channel" class="bbcode_artist">Basic Channel</a> emerged). Chamberlin draws parallels between the compositional techniques used by producers such as <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/R')

Starting in the early 1960s as a scruffy underground scene in San Francisco alternative spaces and New York lofts, minimalism spread to become the most popular experimental music style of the late 20th century.','Minimal is short for <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/minimal%20techno" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">minimal techno</a> but also for <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/minimalist" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">minimalist</a> music which is an more or less originally American genre of <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/experimental" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">experimental</a> or <a href="http://www.last.fm/tag/downtown" class="bbcode_tag" rel="tag">downtown</a> music named in the 1960s based mostly in consonant harmony, steady pulse (if not immobile drones), stasis and slow transformation, and often reiteration of musical phrases or smaller units such as figures, motifs, and cells. Starting in the early 1960s as a scruffy underground scene in San Francisco alternative spaces and New York lofts, minimalism spread to become the most popular experimental music style of the late 20th century. The movement originally involved dozens of composers, although only four<a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Terry+Riley" class="bbcode_artist">Terry Riley</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Steve+Reich" class="bbcode_artist">Steve Reich</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Philip+Glass" class="bbcode_artist">Philip Glass</a>, and, less visibly if more seminally, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/La+Monte+Young" class="bbcode_artist">La Monte Young</a>emerged to become publicly associated with it in America. In Europe, its chief exponents were <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Louis+Andriessen" class="bbcode_artist">Louis Andriessen</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Karel+Goeyvaerts" class="bbcode_artist">Karel Goeyvaerts</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Michael+Nyman" class="bbcode_artist">Michael Nyman</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Gavin+Bryars" class="bbcode_artist">Gavin Bryars</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Steve+Martland" class="bbcode_artist">Steve Martland</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Henryk+G%C3%B3recki" class="bbcode_artist">Henryk G&oacute;recki</a>, <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/Arvo+P%C3%A4rt" class="bbcode_artist">Arvo P&auml;rt</a>, and <a href="http://www.last.fm/music/John+Tavener" class="bbcode_artist">John Tavener</a>. The term &quot;minimalist music&quot; was derived around 1970 by Michael Nyman from the concept of minimalism, which was earlier applied to the visual arts. For some of the music, especially that which transforms itself according to strict rules, the term &quot;process music&quot; has also been used.')

INSERT INTO WIKI(cle_primaire, id_wiki, datePublication, resume, contenu)values(2297,'2297','22/11/2008','Space age pop is a general and loosely based term for a music genre associated with certain Mexican and American composers and songwriters in the Space Age of the 1950s and 1960s. It is also called bachelor pad music or lounge music. Space age pop was inspired by the zeitgeist of those times, an optimism based on the strong post-war economy and technology boom, and excitement about mankind%27s early forrays into space.','Space age pop is a general and loosely based term for a music genre associated with certain Mexican and American composers and songwriters in the Space Age of the 1950s and 1960s. It is also called bachelor pad music or lounge music. Space age pop was inspired by the zeitgeist of those times, an optimism based on the strong post-war economy and technology boom, and excitement about mankind%27s early forrays into space. Although there is no specific album, date, or year when the genre was born, producer Irwin Chusid identifies its heyday as &quot;roughly 1954 to 1964from the dawn of high-fidelity (hi-fi) to the arrival of the Beatles.&quot;
 
 The music is not limited to a single style, and it is not always easily categorized. There are several styles that can be recognized as an influence: classical composers like Ravel and Debussy; the big bands of the 1940s; and different exotic styles, such as samba, latin, and calypso jazz. Space Age pop is related to the genres of lounge music, exotica, or beautiful music and may be regarded as a precursor to the musical genre of space music.')

INSERT INTO WIKI(cle_primaire, id_wiki, datePublication, resume, contenu)values(2357,'2357','07/10/2010','Chiptune is a style of electronic music where all sounds are created using computer or video game console sound chips. More recently, the term has also been used to describe music that sounds like genuine chip music but that is created using more advanced technology, such as software emulators.  Chips provide a small number of channels to work with, each creating a different sound wave.  For example, the chip in the Nintendo Entertainment System has 5 channels: two pulse waves...','Chiptune is a style of electronic music where all sounds are created using computer or video game console sound chips. More recently, the term has also been used to describe music that sounds like genuine chip music but that is created using more advanced technology, such as software emulators.
 
 Chips provide a small number of channels to work with, each creating a different sound wave.  For example, the chip in the Nintendo Entertainment System has 5 channels: two pulse waves, one triangle wave, one white noise channel, and one DPCM channel which was also capable of pulse-code modulation (PCM) sound.  Composers developed techniques to overcome limitations of the chips, such as using fast arpeggios to mimic chords.
 
 Now that chiptunes can be emulated on more advanced technology, their creation has become more widespread into an underground culture of amateur composers.')
